<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A

Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are unaudited. It is the
opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of a normal recurring
nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, and management's discussion and analysis of financial condition and results of
operations, which appear in the Company's Annual Report to Shareholders and which are incorporated by reference into the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. The Company's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery; U.S. Snacks;
U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America
reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously
reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. Also, in connection with the new global organizational structure, Kraft, in
March&nbsp;2004, changed the legal name of one of its subsidiaries, Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc., to Kraft Foods Global,&nbsp;Inc. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Certain
prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform with the current year's presentation, due primarily to the new global organizational structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;123,
"Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which does not result in compensation cost for stock options. The market value at date of grant of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock is
recorded as compensation expense over the period of restriction. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004 and 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock to eligible employees, giving them in most instances all of the rights
of shareholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber the shares and rights. The shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if certain employment conditions are not
met. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million restricted Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S. based employees and also issued to eligible
non-U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.9&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on most of the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2007. The
market value per restricted share or right was $32.23 on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded
pre-tax compensation expense related to restricted stock and rights of $52&nbsp;million and $27&nbsp;million, respectively, for the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30,
2004, and $27&nbsp;million and $16&nbsp;million, respectively, for the six months and three </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>10</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was
$261&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to restricted stock, at June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company had stock-based employee compensation plans that permit the issuance of stock options to employees. The Company applies the
recognition and measurement principles of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25, "Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and related Interpretations in accounting for stock options
within those plans. No compensation expense for employee stock options is reflected in net earnings, as all stock options granted under those plans had an exercise price equal to the market value of
the common stock on the date of grant. The following table illustrates the effect on net earnings and earnings per share ("EPS") if the Company had applied the fair value recognition provisions of
SFAS No.&nbsp;123 to measure stock-based compensation expense for outstanding stock option awards for the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003: </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=11,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=1000752,FOLIO='11',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DM3598A.;9',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dm3598_1_12"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Restructuring Program:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost structure,
and optimizing capacity
utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 through 2006, the
Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including an estimated range of
$750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, pre-tax charges under the restructuring program of $408&nbsp;million and $129&nbsp;million, respectively, were
recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. These charges resulted from the 2004 announcement of the closing of ten plants, the termination of
co-manufacturing agreements and the commencement of a number of workforce reduction programs. Approximately $137&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges incurred during the first
six months of 2004 will result in cash payments. In addition, the Company announced the planned closure of two additional plants as of June&nbsp;30, 2004. The majority of the restructuring charges
for these two plants, which are located within Europe, will be recorded upon local regulatory approval of the plant closures, which is expected in the second half of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pre-tax
restructuring liability activity for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first six months of 2004, as part
of the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,600 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings. Other costs
incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of co-manufacturing agreements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $10&nbsp;million and $9&nbsp;million, respectively, of pre-tax implementation costs associated
with the restructuring program in cost of sales on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. These costs include the discontinuance of certain product lines and other incremental costs
related to the closure of facilities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, during the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash
pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States and certain brands in Mexico. This charge was recorded as asset impairment
and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3. Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
June&nbsp;30, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. owned approximately 84.9% of the Company's outstanding shares of capital stock. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s subsidiary, Altria Corporate
Services,&nbsp;Inc., provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary, corporate affairs,
information technology and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a management fee, were </FONT></P>

and $165&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003, respectively, and $84&nbsp;million and $82&nbsp;million for the three months ended

Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;4. Acquisitions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first six months
of 2004 and 2003, total purchases of businesses, net of acquired cash were $130&nbsp;million and $83&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;6. Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of damages are sought. While
the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's consolidated
financial position or results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and
divestiture activities, approximated $28&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2013, with $5&nbsp;million expiring through June&nbsp;30, 2005. The Company is
required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has a liability of $21&nbsp;million on its
condensed consolidated balance sheet at June&nbsp;30, 2004, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Non-amortizable
intangible assets are substantially comprised of brand names purchased through the Nabisco acquisition. Amortizable intangible assets consist primarily of certain trademark
licenses and non-compete agreements. Pre-tax amortization expense for intangible assets was $6&nbsp;million and $5&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30,
2004 and 2003, respectively, and $4&nbsp;million and $3&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003, respectively. Amortization expense for each of the next five years is
currently estimated to be approximately $12&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Other,
above, includes the reclassification to goodwill of certain amounts previously classified as indefinite life intangible assets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;8. Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
Global,&nbsp;Inc. and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments for
Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp;
Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in
North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which
were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. The Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed
herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the business performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of
segment profitability reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;9. Financial Instruments:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. At June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company was hedging forecasted
transactions for periods not exceeding the next fourteen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the
consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

activities affected accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses), net of income taxes, as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10. Benefit Plans:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued a revised SFAS No.&nbsp;132, "Employers' Disclosures about Pensions and Other Postretirement Benefits." In the first
quarter of 2004, the Company adopted the new interim-period disclosure requirements of this pronouncement relating to net periodic benefit cost and employer contributions to benefit plans, except for
certain interim-period disclosures about non-U.S. plans which are not required until after December&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company sponsors noncontributory defined benefit pension plans covering substantially all U.S. employees. Pension coverage for employees of the Company's non-U.S. subsidiaries is
provided, to the extent deemed appropriate, through separate plans, many of which are governed by local statutory requirements. In </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>19</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>addition,
the Company's U.S. and Canadian subsidiaries provide health care and other benefits to substantially all retired employees. Health care benefits for retirees outside the United States and
Canada are generally covered through local government plans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the United States enacted into law the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization Act of 2003 (the "Act"). The Act establishes a prescription drug benefit under
Medicare, known as
"Medicare Part&nbsp;D," and a federal subsidy to sponsors of retiree health care benefit plans that provide a benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position No.&nbsp;106-2, "Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization
Act of 2003" ("FSP 106-2"). FSP 106-2 requires companies to account for the effect of the subsidy on benefits attributable to past service as an actuarial experience gain and
as a reduction of the service cost component of net postretirement health care costs for amounts attributable to current service, if the benefit provided is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare
Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company has elected to adopt FSP 106-2 prospectively in the third quarter of 2004. The impact for the second half of 2004 will be to reduce net postretirement health care costs and to
increase net earnings by approximately $20&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Description of the Company  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States. At
June&nbsp;30, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 97.9% of the combined voting power of Kraft's outstanding capital stock and owned approximately 84.9% of the outstanding shares of Kraft's capital
stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
Global,&nbsp;Inc. (formerly known as Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc.) and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and
Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are
organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp;
Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>

following executive summary is intended to provide highlights of the Discussion and Analysis that follows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The unfavorable impact of asset impairment, exit and implementation costs on net earnings and diluted EPS is due to the following: </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program. As part of this program,
the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to
$1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, including an estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. The Company recorded pre-tax asset impairment and
exit costs of $408&nbsp;million for this program. In addition, the Company also recorded $10&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs, in cost of sales, associated with the
restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Intangible Asset Impairment Charge</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;During the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of its goodwill and intangible
assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States
and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Lower Effective Income Tax Rate</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 1.2&nbsp;percentage points to 33.9%,
reflecting the reversal of tax accruals that are no longer required due to tax events that occurred during the first six months of 2004. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Currency</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The favorable currency impact on net earnings and diluted EPS is due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar versus the euro
and the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Operations</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The decrease in results from operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial reflecting higher commodity costs, increased promotional programs and higher benefit costs.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial reflecting higher costs, including benefits, promotional programs and infrastructure investment in developing markets. </FONT></DD></DL>

<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=23,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=716229,FOLIO='23',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DS3598A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-AUG-2004;11:07' -->

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
unfavorable impact of asset impairment, exit and implementation costs on net earnings and diluted EPS is due to the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;As discussed above, during the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded pre-tax asset
impairment and exit costs of $129&nbsp;million for its restructuring program. In addition, the Company recorded $9&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs, in cost of sales,
associated with the restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Currency</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The favorable currency impact on net earnings and diluted EPS is due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar versus the euro
and the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Operations</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The decrease in results from operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial reflecting higher commodity costs, increased promotional programs and higher benefits costs.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial reflecting higher costs, including benefits and promotional programs, and unfavorable mix. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see the Consolidated Operating Results and Operating Results by Business Segment sections of the following Discussion and Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>2004 Projected Results</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In July&nbsp;2004, the Company lowered its 2004 full-year diluted EPS guidance range by $0.08 per share
to $1.55 to $1.62, due primarily to higher commodity costs, particularly dairy, that the Company does not expect to fully recover from pricing actions in 2004. Cheese costs, which reached
unprecedented highs earlier in the quarter declined to more historical levels by the end of June. The projected 2004 EPS includes anticipated charges of $0.30 from asset impairment, exit and
implementation costs. The projected diluted EPS also reflects an expected income tax rate of 33% for the year due to the resolution of certain U.S. and foreign tax matters. The factors described in
the section entitled </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> of the following Discussion and Analysis represent continuing risks to these projections. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Discussion and Analysis  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is subject to a number of challenges that may adversely affect its businesses. These challenges, which are discussed below and under the "Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements"
section, include: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>fluctuations
in commodity prices;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>movements
of foreign currencies against the U.S. dollar;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitive
challenges in various products and markets, including price gaps with competitor products and the increasing price-consciousness of consumers; </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>24</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=24,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=461617,FOLIO='24',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DS3598A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-AUG-2004;11:07' -->
<A NAME="page_ds3598_1_25"> </A>
<UL>
<UL>
</UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
rising cost environment;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
trend toward increasing consolidation in the retail trade and consequent inventory reductions;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
growing presence of hard discount retailers, primarily in Europe, with an emphasis on own label products;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>changing
consumer preferences, including low-carbohydrate diet trends;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitors
with different profit objectives and less susceptibility to currency exchange rates; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>consumer
concerns about food safety, quality and health, including concerns about genetically modified organisms, trans-fatty acids and obesity. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>To
confront these challenges, the Company continues to take steps to build the value of its brands, to improve its food business portfolio with new product and marketing initiatives, to reduce costs
through productivity and to address consumer concerns about food safety, quality and health. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced its adoption of a four-point plan to achieve sustainable growth. The first element of the plan is to build brand value by continuing to
improve its products, to use more value-added packaging, to develop innovative new products, to manage price gaps effectively and to build closer relationships with consumers. The Company anticipates
$500 to $600&nbsp;million of increased spending in 2004 over 2003 to manage price gaps, to increase media presence, to drive growth in developing markets and non-measured channels, to
enhance brand equity and to support new products. During the first six months of 2004, the Company increased in-market spending by approximately $245&nbsp;million versus the first six
months of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
second element of the plan is to accelerate the shift in the Company's brand portfolio to address growing consumer demand including products to meet their health and wellness concerns and their
desire for convenience. The Company is reducing trans-fat in its products, identifying its products that are low in carbohydrates, introducing more sugar-free products, and
emphasizing positive nutrition products. The Company is addressing convenience needs by offering more convenient packaging, such as single-serve and resealable packaging, and products requiring
reduced preparation. The Company is also offering packaging that is customized to suit the needs of growing alternate channels of distribution such as supercenters, mass merchandisers, drugstores and
club stores. The Company also plans to shift its portfolio to reflect changing demographics, for example, by expanding the availability of Hispanic products and bilingual packaging. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
third component of the plan is to expand the Company's global scale through international growth, particularly in developing markets. These markets account for approximately 84% of the world's
population and 30% of its packaged food consumption, but only 11% of the Company's 2003 net revenues. The plan calls for the Company to capture the growth potential of its core categories in markets
where it has operations and to expand its core categories into new markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
the final component of its plan, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost
structure, and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions.
From 2004 through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including an
estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $437&nbsp;million and $129&nbsp;million, respectively, of asset impairment and exit costs on its condensed
consolidated statements of earnings. During the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, these pre-tax charges were composed of $408&nbsp;million of costs </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=25,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=884409,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DS3598A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-AUG-2004;11:07' -->
<A NAME="page_ds3598_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>under
the restructuring program and $29&nbsp;million of impairment charges relating to intangible assets. During the second quarter of 2004, all of the pre-tax charges related to the
restructuring program. These charges resulted from the 2004 announcement of the closing of ten plants, the termination of co-manufacturing agreements and the commencement of a number of
workforce reduction programs. Approximately $137&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges incurred during the first six months of 2004 will result in cash payments. In addition, the Company
announced the planned closure of two additional plants as of June&nbsp;30, 2004. The majority of the restructuring charges for these two plants, which are located within Europe, will be recorded
upon local regulatory approval of the plant closures, which is expected in the second half of 2004. During the first quarter of 2004, the Company also completed its annual review of goodwill and
intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the
United States and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pre-tax
restructuring liability activity for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first six months of 2004, as part
of the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,600 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings. Other costs
incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of co-manufacturing agreements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $10&nbsp;million and $9&nbsp;million, respectively, of pre-tax implementation costs associated
with the restructuring program in cost of sales on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. These costs include the discontinuance of certain product lines and other incremental costs
related to the closure of facilities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, the Company expects to spend approximately $140&nbsp;million in capital over the next three years to implement the restructuring program, including approximately $50&nbsp;million in
2004. Cost savings as a result of the restructuring program are expected to be approximately $120&nbsp;million to $140&nbsp;million in 2004, and are anticipated to reach approximately
$400&nbsp;million by 2006, all of which are expected to be used in supporting brand-building initiatives. Cost savings during the first six months of 2004 were approximately $40&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility and intensive price competition, and can influence consumer and trade buying patterns. The Company's businesses are subject to
fluctuating commodity costs, including dairy, coffee and cocoa costs. During the first six months of 2004, the Company's commodity costs on average have been higher than those incurred in 2003 (most
notably dairy, soybean oil, pork and coffee), and have adversely affected earnings. Dairy costs rose to historical highs during the first six months of 2004, but subsequently moderated to historical
levels. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
the ordinary course of business, the Company is subject to many influences that can impact the timing of sales to customers, including the timing of holidays and other annual or special events,
seasonality of certain products, significant weather conditions, timing of Company and customer incentive programs, customer inventory reduction programs, Company initiatives to improve supply chain
efficiency, including efforts to </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=26,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=951639,FOLIO='26',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DS3598A.;9',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-AUG-2004;11:07' -->
<A NAME="page_ds3598_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>align
product shipments more closely with consumption by shifting some of its customer marketing programs to a consumption based approach, financial situations of customers and general economic
conditions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first six months
of 2004 and 2003, total purchases of businesses, net of acquired cash were $130&nbsp;million and $83&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2003, the Company had operations and plants or sold products to third-party distributors located in 15 Middle East countries (as defined by the U.S. Department of State, Bureau of Near Eastern
Affairs), including a biscuit business acquired during 2003 in Egypt. In the region, the Company had operations and plants in three countries (Egypt, Morocco and, through a majority owned joint
venture, Saudi Arabia). In addition, the Company sold products to third-party distributors located in 12 of these countries (Algeria, Bahrain, Israel, Jordan, Kuwait, Lebanon, Oman, Qatar, Syria,
Tunisia, United Arab Emirates and Yemen). Revenue generated from operations or sales to the third-party distributors in the Middle East was approximately $230&nbsp;million in 2003 representing 3.3%
of the net revenues of the Europe, Middle East and Africa segment. In 2004, the Company continues to have operations and plants or to sell products to third-party distributors in these countries,
except for Syria, where the Company ceased sales to the third-party distributor early in the year. In addition, in 2004, the Company entered into agreements with third parties for the resale of the
Company's products into Iraq, Libya and Syria. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2003, the Company was advised by the Fort Worth District Office of the Securities and Exchange Commission ("SEC") that the staff is considering recommending that the SEC bring a
civil injunctive action against the Company charging it with aiding and abetting Fleming Companies ("Fleming") in violations of the securities laws. District staff alleges that a Company employee, who
received a similar notice, signed documents requested by Fleming, which Fleming used in order to accelerate its revenue recognition. The notice does not contain any allegations or statements regarding
the Company's accounting for transactions with Fleming. The Company believes that it properly recorded the transactions in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United
States. The Company has submitted a response to the staff indicating why it believes that no enforcement action should be brought against it. The Company is cooperating fully with the SEC with respect
to this matter and the SEC's investigation of Fleming. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;8. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general
corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the
business performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 2004  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 with the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 2.1%, due primarily to acquisitions and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment, partially offset by the impact of divested
businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $698&nbsp;million (4.6%), due primarily to favorable currency ($543&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($99&nbsp;million), the impact of acquisitions ($69&nbsp;million)
and higher net pricing ($51&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing, partially offset by increased promotional spending), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses
($64&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income decreased $885&nbsp;million (28.4%), due primarily to pre-tax charges in 2004 for asset impairment and exit costs ($437&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher
pricing ($303&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($172&nbsp;million, including higher
benefit costs), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($34&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), the impact of divested businesses ($12&nbsp;million) and the 2004 implementation costs
associated with the restructuring program, partially offset by favorable currency ($61&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($18&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $543&nbsp;million and operating income by $61&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and
the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $19&nbsp;million, due primarily to lower average debt outstanding. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>30</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=30,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=965897,FOLIO='30',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DU3598A.;10',USER='MWEINST',CD=';6-AUG-2004;12:24' -->
<A NAME="page_du3598_1_31"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 1.2&nbsp;percentage points to 33.9%, reflecting the reversal of tax accruals that are no longer required due to tax events that occurred
during the first six months of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $1,258&nbsp;million decreased $539&nbsp;million (30.0%), due primarily to lower operating income, partially offset by a lower effective tax rate. Diluted and basic EPS, which were
both $0.73, decreased by 29.8%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 2004  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 with the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 3.6%, due primarily to acquisitions in the U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery segment and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment,
partially offset by the impact of divested businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $364&nbsp;million (4.6%), due primarily to favorable currency ($237&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($56&nbsp;million), the impact of acquisitions ($55&nbsp;million)
and higher net pricing ($49&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven price increases, partially offset by higher promotional spending), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses
($33&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income decreased $386&nbsp;million (23.7%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($169&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), pre-tax charges in 2004 for asset impairment and exit costs ($129&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($114&nbsp;million,
including higher marketing and benefit costs), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($9&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures, partially offset by favorable
currency ($26&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $237&nbsp;million and operating income by $26&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and
the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $698&nbsp;million decreased $251&nbsp;million (26.4%), due primarily to lower operating income. Diluted and basic EPS, which were both $0.41, decreased by 25.5%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 3.0%, due primarily to acquisitions in the U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery segment and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment,
partially offset by a decline in the U.S. Convenient Meals segment and U.S. Snacks segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $337&nbsp;million (3.1%), due primarily to favorable currency ($112&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($106&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($71&nbsp;million,
reflecting commodity-driven price increases, partially offset by increased promotional spending) and the impact of acquisitions ($48&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $704&nbsp;million (26.9%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exits costs ($301&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs,
net of higher pricing ($269&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($145&nbsp;million, including
higher benefit costs), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($24&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program, partially
offset by higher volume/mix ($26&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($18&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 5.3%, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and gains in
enhancers, coffee and desserts, partially offset by a decline in cereals. Beverages volume </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>32</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=32,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=282105,FOLIO='32',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DW3598A.;5',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dw3598_1_33"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>increased,
due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and new product introductions. In desserts, volume increased, due primarily to higher shipments of sugar-free,
ready-to-eat desserts and frozen toppings. Volume also increased in enhancers, primarily salad dressings and mayonnaise, and in coffee, due to increased marketing spending and
strong performance in supercenters. In cereals, volume declined driven by health and wellness concerns, which impacted the category, and the timing of new product introductions relative to competitive
entries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $2&nbsp;million (0.1%), due primarily to the impact of acquisitions ($39&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower pricing and increased promotional spending
($24&nbsp;million) and unfavorable volume/mix ($13&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $136&nbsp;million (12.8%), due primarily to unfavorable costs and higher promotional spending ($63&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs), higher
marketing, administration and research costs ($56&nbsp;million), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($19&nbsp;million), unfavorable volume/mix and higher
benefit costs, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Snacks</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.1%, as lower biscuits and confectionery volume was essentially offset by higher salted snacks volume. In
biscuits, volume declined, as consumer health and wellness concerns continued to affect consumption. Confectionery volume also declined due to category softness, timing of new product introductions
and increased competitive activity. Salted snacks volume increased due to consumer nutrition trends and marketing programs in nuts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $38&nbsp;million (1.6%), due primarily to lower volume/mix ($52&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($14&nbsp;million, including the absence of high product
returns associated with new products incurred in the prior year, partially offset by increased promotional spending). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $299&nbsp;million (64.0%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($185&nbsp;million), higher marketing,
administration and research costs ($52&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($34&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($22&nbsp;million, driven by higher commodity costs and
increased promotional spending), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program and higher benefit costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.6%, due primarily to the impact of acquisitions and higher
volume in foodservice and cheese. Volume in the foodservice business increased, due primarily to an acquisition of a beverage business in 2004 and higher shipments to national accounts. In cheese,
volume also increased, benefiting from increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $327&nbsp;million (10.0%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($147&nbsp;million), favorable currency ($112&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of higher promotional
reinvestment spending in cheese ($61&nbsp;million), and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $229&nbsp;million (34.9%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($164&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($89&nbsp;million), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($27&nbsp;million, including higher benefit
costs) and higher marketing, administration and research costs ($23&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($57&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($18&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Convenient Meals</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.4%, due primarily to lower shipments in meals, partially offset by gains in meats. In meals,
volume declined due to the discontinuation of certain product lines in the second half of 2003. Meats volume increased driven by higher consumption of cold cuts, supported by higher investment
spending. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>33</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=33,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=289197,FOLIO='33',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DW3598A.;5',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dw3598_1_34"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $46&nbsp;million (2.2%), due primarily to favorable volume/mix ($24&nbsp;million), higher pricing ($20&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing in meats and
pizza) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $40&nbsp;million (9.4%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($20&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($14&nbsp;million), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs and higher fixed manufacturing
costs ($7&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by favorable volume/mix ($11&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
decreased 0.5%, due primarily to the impact of the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, as well as price competition and trade inventory
reductions in several markets, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $361&nbsp;million (8.1%), due primarily to favorable currency ($431&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of
divestitures ($64&nbsp;million), increased promotional spending, net of higher pricing ($20&nbsp;million) and lower volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $184&nbsp;million (30.7%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($136&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs and
increased promotional spending ($44&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($27&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs and infrastructure investment in developing
markets) and the impact of divestitures ($12&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable currency ($43&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 1.3%, due primarily to the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese
business in Europe in 2003, price competition and trade inventory reductions in France and Russia, partially offset by volume growth in Italy and the United Kingdom and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>34</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=34,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=297545,FOLIO='34',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DW3598A.;5',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dw3598_1_35"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Beverages
volume declined, driven by price competition on coffee in France and lower shipments of refreshment beverages in the Middle East. Cheese volume also declined, impacted by the divestiture of
a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, partially offset by increased cream cheese shipments in Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom. Convenient meals volume declined, impacted by the
divestiture of a rice business in Europe in 2003. In grocery, volume increased due primarily to an acquisition in Egypt. Snacks volume also increased, as gains in biscuits, benefiting from
acquisitions, and new confectionery product introductions across the segment, were partially offset by price competition and trade inventory reductions in Russia. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $302&nbsp;million (9.3%), due primarily to favorable currency ($377&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of
divestitures ($64&nbsp;million) and lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($37&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $127&nbsp;million (29.7%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($113&nbsp;million), lower pricing and
increased promotional spending, net of favorable costs ($26&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($25&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs as well as
infrastructure investment in Eastern Europe) and the impact of divestitures ($12&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable currency ($46&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.5%, due primarily to gains in Argentina, Brazil, China and Venezuela, partially
offset by declines in Mexico and Southeast Asia. Snacks volume increased in Argentina, Brazil and China, aided by new product introductions, and growth in Venezuela, due to the 2003 national strike.
Cheese volume increased, due primarily to gains across several markets, including Australia and the Philippines. In grocery, volume also increased due primarily to the 2003 national strike in
Venezuela. Beverages volume declined, impacted by price competition in Mexico, partially offset by gains in China, benefiting from marketing and new product development programs in refreshment
beverages. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $59&nbsp;million (4.9%), due primarily to favorable currency ($54&nbsp;million) and higher pricing ($17&nbsp;million, reflecting devaluation-driven cost increases,
partially offset by increased promotional spending), partially offset by unfavorable volume/mix ($12&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $57&nbsp;million (33.1%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($23&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net
of higher pricing ($18&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending) and unfavorable volume/mix ($11&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 4.9%, due primarily to acquisitions in the U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery segment and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $204&nbsp;million (3.7%), due primarily to higher net pricing ($69&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing in cheese, meats and foodservice, partially offset by
increased promotional spending), higher volume/mix ($49&nbsp;million), the impact of acquisitions ($46&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($40&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $277&nbsp;million (20.7%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($144&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($114&nbsp;million, including higher marketing and benefit costs), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset
impairment and exits costs ($39&nbsp;million), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($9&nbsp;million) and higher benefit costs, partially offset by higher
volume/mix ($17&nbsp;million) and favorable currency. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 10.2%, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and increased
shipments in enhancers and coffee, partially offset by a decline in cereals. Beverages volume increased, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business, new product introductions and
growth in non-measured channels. In coffee, volume increased, benefiting from increased promotional spending. Enhancers volume also increased, due primarily to higher shipments in
mayonnaise and barbecue sauce.
In cereals, volume declined due primarily to increased competitive activity and health and wellness concerns on the category. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $13&nbsp;million (0.8%), due primarily to the impact of acquisitions ($39&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix, partially offset by lower pricing and higher promotional
spending ($35&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $74&nbsp;million (13.5%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($48&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs ($37&nbsp;million,
including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($4&nbsp;million) and higher benefit costs, partially
offset by higher volume/mix ($4&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>36</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=36,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=829762,FOLIO='36',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DW3598A.;5',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dw3598_1_37"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Snacks</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.2%, due primarily to lower confectionery volume, partially offset by higher salted snacks volume.
Confectionery volume declined, due primarily to category softness, the timing of new products and increased competitive activity. Salted snacks volume increased due to consumer nutrition trends and
increased marketing spending in nuts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $17&nbsp;million (1.4%), due primarily to lower volume/mix ($30&nbsp;million) and higher promotional spending, partially offset by the absence of high product returns
associated with new products incurred in the prior year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $69&nbsp;million (27.4%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($39&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($19&nbsp;million), the
2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($9&nbsp;million) and the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($8&nbsp;million), partially
offset by the absence of high product returns associated with new products incurred in the prior year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.2%, due primarily to higher volume in foodservice, cheese and
Canada. Volume in the foodservice business increased, driven by higher shipments to national accounts and the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business. In cheese, volume increased due primarily to
share gains resulting from increased promotional spending. Canada volume also increased, aided by new product introductions in beverages. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $169&nbsp;million (10.0%), due primarily to higher foodservice and cheese pricing, net of higher promotional reinvestment spending in cheese ($68&nbsp;million), higher
volume/mix ($54&nbsp;million), favorable currency ($40&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $122&nbsp;million (35.7%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($98&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), the 2004
pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($27&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($15&nbsp;million) and higher fixed manufacturing costs
($12&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($24&nbsp;million) and favorable currency. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Convenient Meals</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.2%, due primarily to higher shipments in meats, partially offset by declines in meals and pizza.
Meats volume increased driven by higher consumption of cold cuts and hot dogs, which benefited from increased marketing spending. In meals, volume declined due to the discontinuation of certain
product lines in the second half of 2003. Pizza volume declined, due primarily to increased competitive activity. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $39&nbsp;million (3.8%), due primarily to higher pricing and lower promotional spending ($23&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing in meats and pizza) and higher
volume/mix ($16&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $12&nbsp;million (6.0%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($12&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs ($7&nbsp;million,
including higher commodity costs, partially offset by higher pricing and lower promotional spending) and higher benefit costs, partially offset by higher volume/mix ($8&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
decreased 0.2%, due primarily to the impact of the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, price competition, trade inventory reductions and the
transportation strike in Norway, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions and growth in developing markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $160&nbsp;million (6.8%), due primarily to favorable currency ($197&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($9&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of
divestitures ($33&nbsp;million) and lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($20&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $114&nbsp;million (33.6%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($90&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs
($29&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending), lower volume/mix and the impact of divestitures, partially offset by favorable currency ($19&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.8%, due primarily to the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese
business in Europe in 2003, and a decline in some Western European markets, particularly France and the Nordic region, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions. Beverages volume declined, driven
by coffee price competition and market softness in France. Cheese volume also declined, impacted by the divestiture of a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, partially offset by increased
cream cheese shipments in Italy and Germany. In convenient meals, volume declined, impacted by the divestiture of a rice business in Europe in 2003. Snacks volume increased, as gains in biscuits,
benefiting from acquisitions, were partially offset by a decline in confectionery, reflecting price competition and trade inventory reductions in Russia and a national transportation strike in Norway.
In grocery, volume increased due primarily to an acquisition in Egypt. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>38</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=38,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=272869,FOLIO='38',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DY3598A.;4',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dy3598_1_39"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $135&nbsp;million (8.0%), due primarily to favorable currency ($169&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix ($13&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions, partially offset
by the impact of divestitures ($33&nbsp;million) and lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($23&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $89&nbsp;million (38.4%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($81&nbsp;million), lower pricing and
higher promotional spending ($23&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures, partially offset by favorable currency ($20&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.7%, due primarily to gains in both the Latin America and Asia Pacific regions.
Cheese volume increased, due primarily to gains across several markets, including Australia and the Philippines. In beverages, volume declined, impacted by price competition in Mexico, partially
offset by gains in Puerto Rico, Brazil and China. Snacks volume was in-line with the prior year, as increased confectionery shipments in Argentina and Brazil were offset by a decline in
biscuits volume in Venezuela and Southeast Asia. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $25&nbsp;million (3.8%), due primarily to favorable currency ($28&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, partially offset by unfavorable volume/mix and higher promotional
spending. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $25&nbsp;million (23.4%), due primarily to unfavorable volume/mix ($10&nbsp;million), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs
($9&nbsp;million) and unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($9&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Financial Review</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by Operating Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2004, net cash provided by operating activities was $1.3&nbsp;billion compared with $1.6&nbsp;billion in the comparable 2003 period. The decrease in net cash
provided by operating activities is due primarily to lower net earnings and an increase in voluntary pension plan contributions in 2004. The impact of net working capital is unchanged as higher
commodity-driven inventory and accounts payable balances are offset by lower accounts receivable and taxes payable. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in Investing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly investigating
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses that are outside its core categories or that do not meet its growth or profitability targets. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2004, net cash used in investing activities was $465&nbsp;million, compared with $561&nbsp;million in the first six months of 2003. This decrease primarily reflects
lower capital expenditures in 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Capital
expenditures for the first six months of 2004 were $353&nbsp;million, compared with $497&nbsp;million in the first six months of 2003. The Company expects full-year capital
expenditures to be approximately $1.1&nbsp;billion, including capital expenditures estimated at $50&nbsp;million for the restructuring program announced in January&nbsp;2004. These expenditures
are expected to be funded from operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the first six months of 2003, the Company purchased a biscuits business in Egypt. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>39</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=39,EFW="2141487",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=702761,FOLIO='39',FILE='DISK006:[04CHI8.04CHI3598]DY3598A.;4',USER='DINGRAM',CD=';5-AUG-2004;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dy3598_1_40"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in / Provided by Financing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2004, net cash used in financing activities was $1.2&nbsp;billion. During the comparable period of 2003, $268&nbsp;million of net cash was provided by financing
activities. The increase in net cash used in financing activities was due primarily to lower net issuances of short-term debt in 2004 and an increase in the Company's Class&nbsp;A share
repurchases and dividend payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Debt
and Liquidity</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Debt</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company's total debt, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, was $13.3&nbsp;billion at
June&nbsp;30, 2004 and $13.5&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2003. The Company's debt-to-equity ratio was 0.46 at June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 0.47 at December&nbsp;31,
2003. The Company's debt-to-capitalization ratio was 0.31 at June&nbsp;30, 2004 and 0.32 at December&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
June&nbsp;30, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had short-term amounts payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. of $307&nbsp;million and $543&nbsp;million, respectively.
Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
March&nbsp;2004, the Company filed a Form&nbsp;S-3 shelf registration statement with the SEC, which became effective in May&nbsp;2004, under which the Company may sell debt
securities and/or warrants to purchase debt securities in one or more offerings up to a total amount of $4.0&nbsp;billion. The prospectus contained in the registration statement is a combined
prospectus which also covers an additional $250&nbsp;million of unissued principal amount under the previous Form&nbsp;S-3 shelf registration statement filed with the SEC in
April&nbsp;2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Credit Lines</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company maintains revolving credit facilities that have historically been used to support the issuance of commercial
paper. At June&nbsp;30, 2004, credit lines for the Company and the related activity were as follows (in billions): </FONT></P>
